text:
I just made these cookies last night and they are almost gone already.  I followed one reviewer's suggestion of substituting the 1 1/4 cup brown sugar for 1 cup brown sugar, 1/3 cup white sugar and then used a full cup of peanut butter and real butter instead of shortening.  I also baked the cookies at 350 like most people suggested for about 10 minutes.  I only made about 12 cookies from the batch (I like them pretty big) and I flattened the balls of dough out and pressed them with a fork before I baked them.  They are undoubtedly the best PB cookies I've ever had.  I'm making another batch tonight to share with my family!  Follow the substitutions and I GUARANTEE you won't be disappointed!!

text:
This is nearly identical to the recipe I have used for the past 10 years...1/2 a T. less vanilla, and always use butter flavor crisco...bake at 375 for 8 minutes and never over...cool for at least 5 minutes on the cookie sheet before transferring to a cooling rack. I have never had bad luck doing this, and the cookies never last 3 days in my household, with the recipe doubled.

text:
As is, these cookies are just OK. Use a whole cup of peanut butter. Turn the oven down to 350. Use less salt. Replace at least half, if not all of the shortening with butter. Flatten them with a fork, or something. Do these things, and you will have very *excellent* PB cookies. Some people just don't like vanilla; or that much vanilla. My family loves vanilla, and a whole tablespoon is a good thing in my opinion.

text:
I read carefully through the reviews before I made this recipe. A lot of the people increased the peanut butter to a full cup. I did this. I also used butter instead of shortening (I don't usually keep shortening on hand) and super chunky peanut butter, as I like a little texture in my peanut butter cookies. Delicious? Yes. I do believe that the full cup of peanut butter is a must. I did bake mine at 350* as others did and exactly ten minutes was good for me. I tried to pull the cookies off the sheet too soon and they broke up so I ended up letting the cookies sit on the sheet for a minute right out of the oven before taking them off the sheet to cool on the kitchen counter. Moist, flavorful, chewy and just yummy-----and this is coming from a peanut butter cookie hater. I'll make these again. Thanks to those who went before me and left their helpful hints!

these were very tasty and easy to make. I followed the suggestion to use a whole cup of peanut butter instead of 2/3 cup, butter instead of shortening, and 1 cup light brown sugar + 1/4 cup regular sugar instead of 1 1/4 c light brown. I used all natural peanut butter- nothing added, just ground peanuts. The cookies are very good, not too sweet.  I used silpats and they lifted off perfectly after letting them cool 5 min.  Since I use convection bake I lowered the temp to 330 and baked them for 9-10 minutes. will definitely be making these again!

text:
These are very delicious and moist.  I took other's suggestions and used an entire cup of peanut butter.  I chose not to substitute butter for the shortening.  Your cookies will spread and flatten more if you use butter, so be sure to chill the dough first if you make this substitution.  The flavor of this cookie is perfect.  You won't compromise on taste by sticking with shortening. Before baking I rolled in Muscavado Sugar(Sugar in the Raw).  This added nice touch.  I baked at 350 for 10 minutes and they were perfect.

text:
These cookies are GOOD.  They may be the BEST cookies I've ever had.  I'm not big on peanut butter, either.  Ouch!  They are unbelievable.  One note- they took much longer to cook.  After the first 8 minutes I cooked in 2 minute intervals for a total of about 16 minutes.  Hint: if they seem crumbly they need more time.  Also I used a full cup of natural crunchy peanut butter and, of course, substituted butter.  Thick, delicious, beyond moist- excellent flavor.  Do yourself a favor and try this recipe.  YUM!

These are fabulous cookies! I will be using this recipe again. They are very moist and have a delicate peanut butter flavor. Very easy to make, I did make a few adjustments per other reviews I read. I used butter instead of shortening, 1 cup of brown sugar and 1/3 cup of white sugar, also used a full cup of peanut butter. I used a cookie scoop and made criss cross with a fork dipped in white sugar and baked at 350 for 9 1/2 minutes. This recipe made 3 dozen cookies. With these changes, the cookies are superb!

These puppies went really fast once I set them on the table.  I doubled the peanut butter, and used chunky pb.  These cookies were a little bit too sweet to be eaten alone, but a couple fresh out of the oven with a glass of milk was just perfect.  Next time, I'll decrease sugar by a third. text:
I like these cookies a lot! I'd definitely make them again.

I baked the cookies at 350F and found 8 minutes & 30 seconds to be the perfect baking time. I then let them sit for 3 minutes on the stovetop before transferring from cookie sheet to wire rack. 

I used 1/2 cup butter and the 1 cup brown sugar - 1/3 white sugar substitutions. I also added the suggested 1 tbsp honey and used 2 tsp vanilla. I divided the flour into 1/2 cup whole wheat flour and 1 cup unbleached flour. (I use unbleached instead of all-purpose.) I also used natural ground peanut butter. I added 1/2 cup chopped peanuts. I also added 1 cup chocolate chips, but found that to be too many; I'd recommend trying 1/2 cup or 3/4 cup chocolate chips instead.

text:
Can't give five stars because I didn't follow the recipe as written but nevertheless my cookies turned out beautifully. What I did differently: 1) real, softened butter in place of the same amount of shortening 2) used one full cup of peanut butter 3) I used one very scant tablespoon vanilla -- maybe was more like a teaspoon and a half.  I used a heaping medium sized cookie scoop to form balls and rolled them in sugar before using fork to flatten slightly with crisscross pattern. Cooked on a silicone/silpat lined very good cookie sheet in newer convection oven at 340 degrees for about ten minutes each batch. They are beautiful top and bottom and still soft and chewy tonight, hours after making them. They have a nice peanut flavor and are rich tasting thanks to the butter. As mom would warn, don't eat too many of these in one sitting or you'll get an upset tummy (but therein lies the mark of a really good cookie). These made a few dozen, enough to send in a generous portion for my husband's coworkers to enjoy tomorrow. Thanks for the recipe inspiration. This is the best PB cookie recipe I've ever made and will become my go-to PB cookie recipe now.

If you like thick, soft and cakey cookies, this is the peanut butter cookie recipe for you.  I prefer mine a bit thinner, crispier and chewier, so will keep looking.  I thought the cookies had a nice flavor, however.  I used butter instead of shortening, and reduced the salt to 1/2 tsp because my butter was salted.  Also, as another reviewer noted, a tablespoon of vanilla seemed like an awful lot for this size batch of cookies, so I assumed it was a typo and just used 1 teaspoon, which was the perfect amount.

These cookies WERE awesome. I used several suggestions and swapped out 1/4 of the shortening with butter and added peanut butter chips and heath toffee bits. I will be making these cookies again and again. NOTE if the dough is not cold it will be a thinner more spread out cookie.

text:
I followed the recipe, but separated the dough in three sections. In the first, I put white chocolate chips and macadamia nut pieces.  In the second I added peanut butter chips and in the third I added coconut flakes, chocolate chips and almond pieces. Because I added so much to the recipe, I set the oven at 350 instead of 375 and baked the cookies for 8-10 minutes.  I found when baking them at 375, the bottoms burned just a bit. Cookies came out wonderfully.

OMG!...These cookies taste great!  The directions for the recipe was simple to follow.  However, I did take the advice of previous reviewers and modified the following:  1 cup brown sugar, 1/3 cup white sugar, 1 cup peanut butter, 1/2 tsp vanilla extract, oven temp. 350, and finally substituted shortening for 1 stick of butter. country:

text:
In fairness, I made a few minor adjustments based on what I had on hand and some of the suggestions read here so this is more a commentary on my experience and not on Carla's submission.  Her's could very well be better... We really enjoyed them as I made them however.  Here are my modifications. I used butter instead of shortening.  3/4 cup Whole Wheat pastry flour (to TRY to make it a little better for us) and 1 cup regular flour (next time I will try all whole wheat pastry flour) I used 3 TBLSPNS Half & Half in place of milk and cut to 1/2 TBLSPN Vanilla. Dropped by Large spoonfuls & Baked @ 350 for about 12 min. My first batch and largest of the cookies were baked for about 10-11 min and they were almost too moist. I perfer a little tiny bit of crispness to the edge, so I made the rest SLIGHTLY smaller and baked for another min or 2.  YUM~

Well, after looking at the recipe,
thought that I would give it a go...
Ended up putting a full cup of peanut butter, because I couldn't smell the pb after initial amount, and still, they didn't taste like peanut butter.  

Eyebrow went up at the tbsp of vanilla, and tried it, ewwww....

Very wet dough, so I went ahead and added a cup of rolled oats *as I usually do for pb cookies*, and still were wet.  Let it sit in the fridge for and hour, still hard to drop, so I ended up forming them by rolling tablespoonfuls in powdered sugar, then putting it on the pan to mark with a fork. 
Well, without the oats, they spread like crazy, but since I added the oats, I put an extra egg in and omitted the milk. This last batch with the two eggs, 1 tsp of vanilla, 1 cup of pb, and a cup of oats was moist and chewy.  They even held the mark.  Time consuming to roll them in the powdered sugar, but worth it.

text:
These cookies were delicious! They reminded my mom of her aunt's Peanut Butter Kiss Cookies! We used the same exact recipe, except we took about a minute off of the cook time, and while they were still cooling, we stuck Hershey Kisses into the middle and stuck it back into the oven for about a minute. The hersheys will melt a little so they are gooey on the inside but they still keep their shape. These cookies were gone in about 2 days! Also, it's fun to take 2 cookies and mush the kisses together to make sandwich cookies! I am looking forward to using this recipe again!!!

text:
This is a reasonably easy recipe to work with.  I took other people's recommendations and reduced the vanilla to only 1/2 a tablespoon.  I was also rather generous in measuring out the peanut butter.  The cookies turned out well.  The flavour is good, very peanut buttery.  The texture is soft, but I wish they could be more chewy.  As it is, they are soft but a little crumbly.  A friendly reminder to all - be sure to let the cookies cool on the baking sheet.  It helps the cookies to keep their shape while staying soft.  By the way, the cookies taste better on the second day :)

This is by far the best peanut butter cookie recipe and my husband is demanding more!

Very good cookie!  Used other's suggestions and added an extra 1/4 cup of peanut butter and used butter instead of shortening but then had to add 1/4 cup flour.  The dough wouldn't hold together well otherwise.  I also added an extra splash of vanilla which I think made all the difference.  I baked the cookies at 350 for about 9 minutes which made them very soft but all the way done.  Excellent!

text:
Awesome recipe! This is the first time I used this recipe and I totally love it ( so do my daughters and the neighbours :o) We shared some of the cookies out last night and everyone thought they were very delicious! We did make some changes to the recipe as well. We used 1/2c butter instead of shortening, 1 cup brown sugar instead of the 1 1/4c cup, 1 cup of crunchy peanut butter ( just because we had crunchy in the cupboard ), an extra wee bit of vanilla, and we baked them in a fan-forced oven @ 152ish C instead of the 190 stated. Also we found 8 mins was perfect for baking time.. bottoms looked great and none of them burned... VERY HAPPY! This is now a keeper recipe for me and my family for sure. THANKS for posting it :o)I think these would be nice with choc chips or peanut butter chips or even toffee bits, smiles!

text:
These peanut butter cookies were great and easy to make too! :) I think what needs to be added to the preparation of the cookies to make it a better is to roll the cookie dough into balls(after measuring out an approximate tablespoon) then taking a small salad fork and pushing the fork onto the cookie dough balls making the "signature" cross-hatch design on the top of each cookie.  It definitely came out a lot more round that way.  Also, I had to cut back on the baking time a bit since it made the bottoms of the cookies a bit darker than I wanted. Otherwise, awesome recipe!

text:
I just made these cookies for my husband and they are great! I do not even like peanut butter cookies but I like these. I looked at the other reviews and made the same modifications: 
-Use 1 cup of brown sugar
-Use 1/3 cup white sugar 
-Use 1 cup of peanut butter
-Use butter instead of shortening 
-Use a little less vanilla extract
I am very glad I read the reviews before making this. I would give this recipe 4 stars because it had to be modified. The best recipe actually came from the people that commented and not the one copied on here. I like when I can follow a recipe to a T and do not have to make modifications. That just makes the process more complicated. Thank you to all of you who went before me and found out how to make this recipe better so I could have great cookies!

text:
These were very good! I was shocked to see that someone rated them the worst ever. I am not sure what she did wrong but if you follow the recipe accurately, these are delicious! 1 Tablespoon of vanilla was necessary with the amount of flour and balancing out the saltiness of the PB. I added a pinch more salt, a pinch more brown sugar,  instead of using all light brown sugar, I used 1/2 c light brown sugar,  1/2 c dark brown sugar and for the remaining balance  I used  white sugar.  I also added a teaspoon of maple syrup and omitted one teaspoon of milk to compensate (1 tbsp = 3 tsp, FYI). I also used butter-flavored crisco as that was all I had in stock! Very delicious!

None
text:
This cookie was one of the 6 cookie recipes I selected to make for Christmas this year, and my first attempt at traditional peanut butter cookies. A few pointers - buy no salt peanut butter; this will help to regulate the recipe. I purchased a natural smooth peanut butter ("Teddy" brand) and despite it's good quality I found my results a little too salty, and a little oily tasting. Also, I dipped my cookie dough balls in granulated sugar before baking them, and I think this may have been their saving grace. Without that, they certainly would have been too salty and not sweet enough. I added slightly less salt and slightly less vanilla than the recipe called for. I will probably not use this recipe again, however I realize a huge part of making peanut butter cookies is the peanut butter you use, so perhaps I will give it one more chance with a different brand of no-salt peanut butter.

Definately be making these more often.

text:
I liked the texture result of this recipe most of all.  They were a little crisp on the bottom and chewy in the middle, which I love in any cookie.  However as I went through the recipe I suspected that there was too much vanilla, baking soda, and too little flour.  An accomplished chef friend of mine really raved about them, and took some home to his family. If you like old fashioned tasting recipes this one is good because the brown sugar really brings out a molasses taste that reminded me of my great-grandmother's gingersnaps.  But if you want your cookies to taste like the gourmet bakery's down the street, this recipe is not for you.
